        <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">

      <tr>
       <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">
        Religion
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
        Predominantly:
        <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">
         Coptic Orthodox Christianity
        </a>
        .
        <br/>
        Also
        <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Catholic_Church" title="Coptic Catholic Church">
         Coptic Catholicism
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Egypt" title="Protestantism in Egypt">
         Protestants
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The
      <b>
       Copts
      </b>
      are an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethno-religious" title="Ethno-religious">
       ethno-religious
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Serer_Race_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Serer_Race-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      group situated in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Africa_and_the_Middle_East" title="North Africa and the Middle East">
       North Africa and the Middle East
      </a>
      , mainly in the area of modern
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      , where they are the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Egypt" title="Christianity in Egypt">
       Christian denomination
      </a>
      , but also in
      <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
       Sudan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
       Libya
      </a>
      . Christianity was the religion of the vast majority of Egyptians from 400800 A.D. and the majority after the Muslim conquest until the mid-10th century
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Bill_Has_Egypt.27s_Copts_Squirming_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-U.S._Bill_Has_Egypt.27s_Copts_Squirming-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and remains the faith of a significant minority population. Historically they spoke the
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">
       Coptic language
      </a>
      , a direct descendant of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demotic_Egyptian" title="Demotic Egyptian">
       Demotic Egyptian
      </a>
      spoken in the Roman era, but it has been near-extinct and mostly limited to liturgical use since the 18th century. They now speak
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
       Arabic
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Copts in Egypt constitute the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Middle_East" title="Christianity in the Middle East">
       Christian community in the Middle East
      </a>
      , as well as the largest religious minority in the region, accounting for an estimated 10% of the Egyptian population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Christian-Muslim_Gap_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Christian-Muslim_Gap-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most Copts adhere to the
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">
       Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO.2FEgypt.2F_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FCO.2FEgypt.2F-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Catholic_Church" title="Coptic Catholic Church">
       Coptic Catholic Church
      </a>
      , which is an
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">
       Eastern Catholic church
      </a>
      in full communion with the
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
       Catholic Church
      </a>
      , claims 163,000 members.
     </p>
     <table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="394" data-file-width="475" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/CopticLetters.svg/40px-CopticLetters.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/CopticLetters.svg/60px-CopticLetters.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/CopticLetters.svg/80px-CopticLetters.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">
        <b>
         This article contains
         <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">
          Coptic
         </a>
         text.
        </b>
        Without proper
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support#Coptic" title="Help:Multilingual support">
         rendering support
        </a>
        , you may see
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">
         question marks, boxes, or other symbols
        </a>
        instead of Coptic letters.
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
       Name
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Name_of_Egypt" title="Name of Egypt">
       Name of Egypt
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_monks.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1903" data-file-width="2447" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Coptic_monks.jpg/200px-Coptic_monks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Coptic_monks.jpg/300px-Coptic_monks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Coptic_monks.jpg/400px-Coptic_monks.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_monks.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coptic monks between 1898 and 1914.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The word
      <i>
       Copt
      </i>
      was adopted in English in the 17th century, from
      <a href="/wiki/New_Latin" title="New Latin">
       New Latin
      </a>
      <i>
       Coptus, Cophtus
      </i>
      , which is derived from
      <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
       Arabic
      </a>
      collective
      <i>
       <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">
        qub / qib
       </span>
      </i>
      <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
       
      </span>
      "the Copts" with
      <a href="/wiki/Arabic_grammar#nisba" title="Arabic grammar">
       nisba
      </a>
      adjective
      <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">
       <i>
        qub, qib
       </i>
      </span>
      <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
       
      </span>
      , plural
      <i>
       <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">
        aqb
       </span>
      </i>
      <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
       
      </span>
      ; Also
      <i>
       quft, qift
      </i>
      , Arabic
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_labiodental_fricative" title="Voiceless labiodental fricative">
        f
       </a>
       /
      </span>
      representing historical Coptic
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_bilabial_stop" title="Voiceless bilabial stop">
        p
       </a>
       /
      </span>
      . an Arabisation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">
       Coptic
      </a>
      word
      <i>
       kubti
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language#Bohairic" title="Coptic language">
       Bohairic
      </a>
      ) and/or
      <i>
       kuptaion
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language#Sahidic" title="Coptic language">
       Sahidic
      </a>
      ). The Coptic word is in turn an adaptation of the Greek
      <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
       
      </span>
      <i>
       <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Ancient Greek transliteration">
        Aigptios
       </span>
      </i>
      "Egyptian" ultimately related to
      <a href="/wiki/Caphtor" title="Caphtor">
       Caphtor
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The term is thus ultimately derived from the Greek designation of the native Egyptian population in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Egypt" title="Roman Egypt">
       Roman Egypt
      </a>
      (as distinct from Greeks, Romans, Jews, etc.). After the
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Egypt" title="Muslim conquest of Egypt">
       Muslim conquest of Egypt
      </a>
      , it became restricted to those Egyptians adhering to the Christian religion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Greek term for Egypt,
      <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
       
      </span>
      , is itself derived from the
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_language" title="Egyptian language">
       Egyptian language
      </a>
      , but dates to a much earlier period, being attested already in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mycenean_Greek" title="Mycenean Greek">
       Mycenean Greek
      </a>
      as
      <i>
       a
       <sub>
        3
       </sub>
       -ku-pi-ti-jo
      </i>
      (lit. "Egyptian"; used here as a man's name). This Mycenaean form is likely from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Egyptian" title="Middle Egyptian">
       Middle Egyptian
      </a>
      <span lang="egy-Latn" xml:lang="egy-Latn">
       <i>
        wt-k3-pt
       </i>
      </span>
      ("Hut-ka-Ptah"), literally "Estate (or 'House') of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_soul" title="Egyptian soul">
       Spirit
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Ptah" title="Ptah">
       Ptah
      </a>
      " (cf.
      <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_language" title="Akkadian language">
       Akkadian
      </a>
      <span lang="akk-Latn" xml:lang="akk-Latn">
       <i>
        <sup>
         lu
        </sup>
        i-ku-up-ta-a
       </i>
      </span>
      ), the name of the temple complex of the god
      <a href="/wiki/Ptah" title="Ptah">
       Ptah
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Egypt" title="Memphis, Egypt">
       Memphis
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In their own
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">
       Coptic language
      </a>
      , the Copts referred to themselves as
      <i>
       rem en kme
      </i>
      (Sahidic)
      <span class="script-coptic" style="font-family:'New Athena Unicode', 'MPH 2B Damase', 'Arial Coptic', Quivira, Analecta, Antinoou, 'Noto Sans Coptic';">
       
      </span>
      ,
      <i>
       lem en kmi
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language#Fayyumic" title="Coptic language">
       Fayyumic
      </a>
      ),
      <i>
       rem en khmi
      </i>
      (Bohairic)
      <span class="script-coptic" style="font-family:'New Athena Unicode', 'MPH 2B Damase', 'Arial Coptic', Quivira, Analecta, Antinoou, 'Noto Sans Coptic';">
       
      </span>
      , which literally means "people of Egypt" or "Egyptians"; cf.
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_language" title="Egyptian language">
       Egyptian
      </a>
      <i>
       <span lang="egy-Latn" xml:lang="egy-Latn">
        rm n
        <a href="/wiki/Km_(hieroglyph)" title="Km (hieroglyph)">
         kmt
        </a>
       </span>
      </i>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demotic_Egyptian" title="Demotic Egyptian">
       Demotic
      </a>
      <i>
       <span lang="egy-Latn" xml:lang="egy-Latn">
        rmt n km
       </span>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The Arabic word
      <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">
       <i>
        qib
       </i>
      </span>
      "Copt" has also been connected to the Greek name of the town of 
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coptos" title="Coptos">
        Coptos
       </a>
      </i>
      (modern day
      <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">
       <i>
        Qif
       </i>
      </span>
      ; Coptic
      <i>
       Kebt
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Keft
      </i>
      ). It is possible that this association has contributed to making
      <i>
       Copt
      </i>
      the settled form of the name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 20th century, some Egyptian nationalists and intellectuals in the context of
      <a href="/wiki/Pharaonism" title="Pharaonism">
       Pharaonism
      </a>
      began using the term
      <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">
       qub
      </span>
      in the historical sense.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

       <td style="padding:0.2em 0 0.4em">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_cross.svg">
         <img alt="Coptic cross.svg" data-file-height="606" data-file-width="606" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Coptic_cross.svg/165px-Coptic_cross.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Coptic_cross.svg/248px-Coptic_cross.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Coptic_cross.svg/330px-Coptic_cross.svg.png 2x" width="165"/>
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>

     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">
       Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Christianity_in_Egypt" title="History of Christianity in Egypt">
       History of Christianity in Egypt
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:193px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StMarkcoptic.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="376" data-file-width="191" height="376" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/67/StMarkcoptic.jpg" width="191"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StMarkcoptic.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coptic icon of
        <a href="/wiki/Mark_the_Evangelist" title="Mark the Evangelist">
         St. Mark
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Copts are one of the oldest Christian communities in the Middle East. Although integrated in the larger Egyptian nation state, the ethnic Copts have survived as a distinct
      <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Egypt" title="Religion in Egypt">
       religious community
      </a>
      forming around 1020% of the population,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt_20-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO.2FEgypt.2F_21-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FCO.2FEgypt.2F-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_world_factbook.2FEgypt.2F_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_world_factbook.2FEgypt.2F-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPS_News_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IPS_News-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christianpost.com_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-christianpost.com-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtoninstitute.org_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-washingtoninstitute.org-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nlgsolutions1_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nlgsolutions1-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      though estimates vary. They pride themselves on the apostolicity of the Egyptian Church whose founder was the first in an unbroken chain of patriarchs. The main body for 16 centuries has been out of communion with both the Roman Catholic Church (in Rome) and the various Eastern orthodox churches.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_of_the_Christian_Church_in_Egypt">
       Foundation of the Christian Church in Egypt
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      According to ancient tradition,
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      was introduced within present day
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_the_Evangelist" title="Mark the Evangelist">
       Saint Mark
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">
       Alexandria
      </a>
      , shortly after the ascension of
      <a href="/wiki/Christ" title="Christ">
       Christ
      </a>
      and during the reign of the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Emperor" title="Emperor">
       emperor
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">
       Claudius
      </a>
      around 42AD.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The legacy that
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_the_Evangelist" title="Mark the Evangelist">
       Saint Mark
      </a>
      left in
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      was a considerable
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      community in
      <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">
       Alexandria
      </a>
      . From Alexandria,
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      spread throughout
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      within half a century of
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_the_Evangelist" title="Mark the Evangelist">
       Saint Mark
      </a>
      's arrival in
      <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">
       Alexandria
      </a>
      , as is clear from a fragment of the
      <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_John" title="Gospel of John">
       Gospel of John
      </a>
      , written in
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">
       Coptic
      </a>
      , which was found in
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_Egypt" title="Upper Egypt">
       Upper Egypt
      </a>
      and can be dated to the first half of the 2nd century, and the
      <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
       New Testament
      </a>
      writings found in
      <a href="/wiki/Oxyrhynchus" title="Oxyrhynchus">
       Oxyrhynchus
      </a>
      , in
      <a href="/wiki/Middle_Egypt" title="Middle Egypt">
       Middle Egypt
      </a>
      , which date around the year 200AD. In the 2nd century,
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      began to spread to the rural areas, and scriptures were translated into the local language, today known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">
       Coptic language
      </a>
      , but known as the
      <i>
       Egyptian language
      </i>
      at the time. By the beginning of the 3rd century AD,
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christians
      </a>
      constituted the majority of Egypts population, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Alexandria" title="Church of Alexandria">
       Church of Alexandria
      </a>
      was recognized as one of
      <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">
       Christendom
      </a>
      's four Apostolic Sees, second in honor only to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
       Church of Rome
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Alexandria" title="Church of Alexandria">
       Church of Alexandria
      </a>
      is therefore the oldest Christian church in Africa.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Contributions_to_Christianity">
       Contributions to Christianity
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Copts in Egypt contributed immensely to
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      tradition. The Catechetical School of Alexandria was the oldest catechetical school in the world. Founded around 190AD by the scholar
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pantanaeus" title="Pantanaeus">
       Pantanaeus
      </a>
      , the school of Alexandria became an important institution of religious learning, where students were taught by scholars such as
      <a href="/wiki/Athenagoras_of_Athens" title="Athenagoras of Athens">
       Athenagoras
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Clement_of_Alexandria" title="Clement of Alexandria">
       Clement
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Didymus_the_Blind" title="Didymus the Blind">
       Didymus
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Origen" title="Origen">
       Origen
      </a>
      , the father of theology and who was also active in the field of commentary and comparative Biblical studies. However, the scope of this school was not limited to theological subjects; science, mathematics and humanities were also taught there. The question-and-answer method of commentary began there, and 15 centuries before
      <a href="/wiki/Braille" title="Braille">
       Braille
      </a>
      , wood-carving techniques were in use there by blind scholars to read and write.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another major contribution made by the Copts in Egypt to
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      was the creation and organization of
      <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">
       monasticism
      </a>
      . Worldwide Christian monasticism stems, either directly or indirectly, from the Egyptian example. The most prominent figures of the monastic movement were
      <a href="/wiki/Anthony_the_Great" title="Anthony the Great">
       Anthony the Great
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_of_Thebes" title="Paul of Thebes">
       Paul of Thebes
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macarius_the_Great" title="Macarius the Great">
       Macarius the Great
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenouda_the_Archimandrite" title="Shenouda the Archimandrite">
       Shenouda the Archimandrite
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pachomius" title="Pachomius">
       Pachomius the Cenobite
      </a>
      . By the end of the 5th century, there were hundreds of monasteries, and thousands of cells and caves scattered throughout the Egyptian desert. Since then pilgrims have visited the Egyptian
      <a href="/wiki/Desert_Fathers" title="Desert Fathers">
       Desert Fathers
      </a>
      to emulate their spiritual, disciplined lives.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Basil" title="Saint Basil">
       Saint Basil the Great
      </a>
      Archbishop of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesarea_Mazaca" title="Caesarea Mazaca">
       Caesarea Mazaca
      </a>
      , and the founder and organiser of the monastic movement in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" title="Asia Minor">
       Asia Minor
      </a>
      , visited
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      around 357AD and his monastic rules are followed by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Churches" title="Eastern Orthodox Churches">
       Eastern Orthodox Churches
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Jerome" title="Saint Jerome">
       Saint Jerome
      </a>
      , who translated the
      <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">
       Bible
      </a>
      into
      <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
       Latin
      </a>
      , came to
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      while en route to
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      around 400AD and left details of his experiences in his letters.
      <a href="/wiki/Benedict_of_Nursia" title="Benedict of Nursia">
       Saint Benedict
      </a>
      founded the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictine_Order" title="Benedictine Order">
       Benedictine Order
      </a>
      in the 6th century on the model of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Pachomius" title="Saint Pachomius">
       Saint Pachomius
      </a>
      , although in a stricter form.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Ecumenical_Councils">
       The Ecumenical Councils
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The major contributions that the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/See_of_Alexandria" title="See of Alexandria">
       See of Alexandria
      </a>
      has contributed to the establishment of early Christian theology and dogma are attested to by fact that the first three
      <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_council" title="Ecumenical council">
       Ecumenical councils
      </a>
      in the history of
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      were headed by Egyptian patriarchs. The
      <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea" title="First Council of Nicaea">
       Council of Nicaea
      </a>
      (325AD) was presided over by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_of_Alexandria" title="Alexander of Alexandria">
       St. Alexander, Patriarch of Alexandria
      </a>
      , along with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hosius_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Hosius of Crdoba">
       Saint Hosius of Crdoba
      </a>
      . In addition, the most prominent figure of the council was the future
      <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_of_Alexandria" title="Patriarch of Alexandria">
       Patriarch of Alexandria
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Athanasius_of_Alexandria" title="Athanasius of Alexandria">
       Athanasius
      </a>
      , who played the major role in the formulation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nicene_Creed" title="Nicene Creed">
       Nicene Creed
      </a>
      , recited today in most Christian churches of different denominations. One of the council's decisions was to entrust the
      <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_of_Alexandria" title="Patriarch of Alexandria">
       Patriarch of Alexandria
      </a>
      with calculating and annually announcing the exact date of
      <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">
       Easter
      </a>
      to the rest of the Christian churches. The
      <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Constantinople" title="First Council of Constantinople">
       Council of Constantinople
      </a>
      (381AD) was presided over by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timothy_of_Alexandria" title="Timothy of Alexandria">
       Patriarch Timothy of Alexandria
      </a>
      , while the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Ephesus" title="First Council of Ephesus">
       Council of Ephesus
      </a>
      (431AD) was presided over by
      <a href="/wiki/Cyril_of_Alexandria" title="Cyril of Alexandria">
       Cyril of Alexandria
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_Chalcedon">
       Council of Chalcedon
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 451AD, following the
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Chalcedon" title="Council of Chalcedon">
       Council of Chalcedon
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Alexandria" title="Church of Alexandria">
       Church of Alexandria
      </a>
      was divided into two branches. Those who accepted the terms of the Council became known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chalcedonian" title="Chalcedonian">
       Chalcedonians
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melkites" title="Melkites">
       Melkites
      </a>
      . Those who did not abide by the Council's terms were labeled
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Chalcedonian" title="Non-Chalcedonian">
       non-Chalcedonians
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophysites" title="Monophysites">
       Monophysites
      </a>
      and later Jacobites after
      <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Baradaeus" title="Jacob Baradaeus">
       Jacob Baradaeus
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Chalcedonian" title="Non-Chalcedonian">
       non-Chalcedonians
      </a>
      , however, rejected the term
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophysites" title="Monophysites">
       Monophysites
      </a>
      as erroneous and referred to themselves as
      <a href="/wiki/Miaphysitism" title="Miaphysitism">
       Miaphysites
      </a>
      . The majority of the
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">
       Egyptians
      </a>
      belonged to the
      <a href="/wiki/Miaphysitism" title="Miaphysitism">
       Miaphysite
      </a>
      branch, which led to their persecution by the
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
       Byzantines
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Arab_invasion_of_Egypt">
       The Arab invasion of Egypt
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Islamization_of_Egypt" title="Islamization of Egypt">
       Islamization of Egypt
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3710" data-file-width="2374" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg/180px-Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg/270px-Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg/360px-Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kairo_Hanging_Church_BW_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Hanging_Church" title="The Hanging Church">
         The Hanging Church
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Cairo" title="Coptic Cairo">
         Coptic Cairo
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 641AD,
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      was invaded by the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
       Arabs
      </a>
      who faced off with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">
       Byzantine
      </a>
      army, but found little to no resistance from the native Egyptian population. Local resistance by the Egyptians however began to materialize shortly thereafter and would last until at least the 9th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Copts_in_modern_Egypt">
       Copts in modern Egypt
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copts_in_Egypt" title="Copts in Egypt">
       Copts in Egypt
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Egypt" title="Christianity in Egypt">
       Christianity in Egypt
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="391" data-file-width="450" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg/180px-Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg/270px-Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg/360px-Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Copts-with-Nasser-1965.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        President Nasser welcomes a delegation of Coptic bishops (1965)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_flag.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Coptic_flag.svg/180px-Coptic_flag.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Coptic_flag.svg/270px-Coptic_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Coptic_flag.svg/360px-Coptic_flag.svg.png 2x" width="180"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_flag.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Coptic_flag" title="Coptic flag">
         Coptic flag
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Under Muslim rule, Christians were second-class citizens, who paid special taxes, had no access to political power, but were exempt from military service. The Copts were cut off from the main stream of Christianity, but they were allowed to practice their religion unmolested. Their position improved dramatically under the rule of
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">
       Muhammad Ali
      </a>
      in the early 19th century. He abolished the
      <a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">
       Jizya
      </a>
      (a tax on non-Muslims) and allowed Egyptians (Copts) to enroll in the army.
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Cyril_IV_of_Alexandria" title="Pope Cyril IV of Alexandria">
       Pope Cyril IV
      </a>
      , 185461, reformed the church and encouraged broader Coptic participation in Egyptian affairs. Khedive
      <a href="/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha" title="Isma'il Pasha">
       Isma'il Pasha
      </a>
      , in power 186379, further promoted the Copts. He appointed them judges to Egyptian courts and awarded them political rights and representation in government. They flourished in business affairs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Copts participated in the Egyptian national movement for independence and occupied many influential positions. Two significant cultural achievements include the founding of the
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Museum" title="Coptic Museum">
       Coptic Museum
      </a>
      in 1910 and the Higher Institute of Coptic Studies in 1954. Some prominent Coptic thinkers from this period are
      <a href="/wiki/Salama_Moussa" title="Salama Moussa">
       Salama Moussa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Louis_Awad" title="Louis Awad">
       Louis Awad
      </a>
      and Secretary General of the
      <a href="/wiki/Wafd_Party" title="Wafd Party">
       Wafd Party
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Makram_Ebeid" title="Makram Ebeid">
       Makram Ebeid
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1952,
      <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">
       Gamal Abdel Nasser
      </a>
      led some army officers in a coup d'tat against
      <a href="/wiki/Farouk_of_Egypt" title="Farouk of Egypt">
       King Farouk
      </a>
      , which overthrew the Kingdom of Egypt and established a republic.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasser" title="Nasser">
       Nasser
      </a>
      's mainstream policy was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan-Arab" title="Pan-Arab">
       pan-Arab
      </a>
      nationalism and socialism. The ethnic Copts were severely affected by Nasser's nationalization policies, though they represented about 1020% of the population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nisan_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nisan-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition, Nasser's pan-Arab policies undermined the Copts' strong attachment to and sense of identity about their Egyptian pre-Arab, and certainly non-Arab identity which resulted in permits to construct churches to be delayed along with Christian religious courts to be closed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nisan_35-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nisan-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Pharaonism">
       Pharaonism
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Pharaonism" title="Pharaonism">
       Pharaonism
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Many Coptic intellectuals hold to "Pharaonism," which states that Coptic culture is largely derived from pre-Christian, Pharaonic culture, and is not indebted to Greece. It gives the Copts a claim to a deep heritage in Egyptian history and culture. Pharaonism was widely held by Coptic and Muslim scholars in the early 20th century, and it helped bridge the divide between those groups. Most scholars today see Pharaonism as a late development shaped primarily by western
      <a href="/wiki/Orientalism" title="Orientalism">
       Orientalism
      </a>
      , and doubt its validity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Church_affairs">
       Church affairs
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Today, members of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Chalcedonian" title="Non-Chalcedonian">
       non-Chalcedonian
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church" title="Coptic Orthodox Church">
       Coptic Orthodox Church
      </a>
      constitute the majority of the Egyptian Christian population. Mainly through emigration and partly through European, American, and other missionary work and conversions, the Egyptian Christian community now also includes other
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      denominations such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
       Protestants
      </a>
      (known in Arabic as Evangelicals),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
       Roman
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Rite_Catholic" title="Eastern Rite Catholic">
       Eastern Rite Catholics
      </a>
      , and other
      <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      congregations. The term
      <i>
       Coptic
      </i>
      remains exclusive however to the Egyptian natives, as opposed to the Christians of non-Egyptian origins. Some Protestant churches for instance are called "Coptic Evangelical Church", thus helping differentiate their native Egyptian congregations from churches attended by non-Egyptian immigrant communities such as Europeans or Americans.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2005 a group of Coptic activists created a
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_flag" title="Coptic flag">
       flag
      </a>
      to represent Copts worldwide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The last head of the Coptic Orthodox Church,
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Shenouda_III_of_Alexandria" title="Pope Shenouda III of Alexandria">
       Pope Shenouda III of Alexandria
      </a>
      , died 17 March 2012. On 4 November 2012, Bishop Tawadros was chosen as the new pope of Egypt's Coptic Christians. His name was selected from a glass bowl containing the three shortlisted candidates by a blindfolded boy at a ceremony in Cairo's
      <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mark%27s_Coptic_Orthodox_Cathedral,_Cairo" title="Saint Mark's Coptic Orthodox Cathedral, Cairo">
       St Mark's Cathedral
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNANKH-BBC-4NOV2012_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNANKH-BBC-4NOV2012-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Copts_in_modern_Sudan">
       Copts in modern Sudan
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Sudan" title="Copts in Sudan">
       Copts in Sudan
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Sudan" title="Christianity in Sudan">
       Christianity in Sudan
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_cathedral_(Khartoum)_001.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1530" data-file-width="1200" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Coptic_cathedral_%28Khartoum%29_001.jpg/180px-Coptic_cathedral_%28Khartoum%29_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Coptic_cathedral_%28Khartoum%29_001.jpg/270px-Coptic_cathedral_%28Khartoum%29_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Coptic_cathedral_%28Khartoum%29_001.jpg/360px-Coptic_cathedral_%28Khartoum%29_001.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coptic_cathedral_(Khartoum)_001.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Holy Mary Coptic Orthodox Cathedral,
        <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">
         Khartoum
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
         Sudan
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
       Sudan
      </a>
      has a native Coptic minority, although many Copts in Sudan are descended from more recent Egyptian immigrants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Copts in Sudan live mostly in northern cities, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Obeid" title="Al Obeid">
       Al Obeid
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Atbara" title="Atbara">
       Atbara
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dongola" title="Dongola">
       Dongola
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">
       Khartoum
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Omdurman" title="Omdurman">
       Omdurman
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Port_Sudan" title="Port Sudan">
       Port Sudan
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wad_Medani" title="Wad Medani">
       Wad Medani
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They number up to 500,000, or slightly over 1% of the Sudanese population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Due to their advanced education, their role in the life of the country has been more significant than their numbers suggest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They have occasionally faced forced conversion to
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      , resulting in their emigration and decrease in number.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Modern immigration of Copts to Sudan peaked in the early 19th century, and they generally received a tolerant welcome there. However, this was interrupted by a decade of persecution under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Mahdist_Sudan" title="History of Mahdist Sudan">
       Mahdist rule
      </a>
      at the end of the 19th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a result of this persecution, many were forced to relinquish their faith, adopt
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      , and intermarry with the native Sudanese. The
      <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Sudan" title="Anglo-Egyptian Sudan">
       Anglo-Egyptian invasion
      </a>
      in 1898 allowed Copts greater religious and economic freedom, and they extended their original roles as artisans and merchants into trading, banking, engineering, medicine, and the civil service. Proficiency in business and administration made them a privileged minority. However, the return of
      <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">
       militant Islam
      </a>
      in the mid-1960s and subsequent demands by radicals for an
      <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">
       Islamic constitution
      </a>
      prompted Copts to join in public opposition to religious rule.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Gaafar_Nimeiry" title="Gaafar Nimeiry">
       Gaafar Nimeiry
      </a>
      's introduction of Islamic
      <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">
       Sharia
      </a>
      law in 1983 began a new phase of oppressive treatment of Copts, among other non-Muslims.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the overthrow of Nimeiry, Coptic leaders supported a secular candidate in the 1986 elections. However, when the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Islamic_Front" title="National Islamic Front">
       National Islamic Front
      </a>
      overthrew the elected government of
      <a href="/wiki/Sadiq_al-Mahdi" title="Sadiq al-Mahdi">
       Sadiq al-Mahdi
      </a>
      with the help of the military, discrimination against Copts returned in earnest. Hundreds of Copts were dismissed from the civil service and judiciary.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In February 1991, a Coptic pilot working for
      <a href="/wiki/Sudan_Airways" title="Sudan Airways">
       Sudan Airways
      </a>
      was executed for illegal possession of foreign currency.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sudanupdate1_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sudanupdate1-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Before his execution, he had been offered amnesty and money if he converted to
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      , but he refused. Thousands attended his funeral, and the execution was taken as a warning by many Copts, who began to flee the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sudanupdate1_40-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sudanupdate1-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Restrictions on the Copts' rights to Sudanese nationality followed, and it became difficult for them to obtain Sudanese nationality by birth or by naturalization, resulting in problems when attempting to travel abroad. The confiscation of Christian schools and the imposition of an Arab-Islamic emphasis in language and history teaching were accompanied by harassment of Christian children and the introduction of
      <a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">
       hijab
      </a>
      dress laws. A Coptic child was flogged for failing to recite a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koranic" title="Koranic">
       Koranic
      </a>
      verse.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sudanupdate1_40-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-sudanupdate1-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In contrast with the extensive media broadcasting of the Muslim
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friday_prayers" title="Friday prayers">
       Friday prayers
      </a>
      , the radio ceased coverage of the Christian Sunday service. As the civil war raged throughout the 1990s, the government focused its religious fervour on the south. Although experiencing discrimination, the Copts and other long-established Christian groups in the north had fewer restrictions than other types of Christians in the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">
       south
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Today, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coptic_Church" title="Coptic Church">
       Coptic Church
      </a>
      in Sudan is officially registered with the government, and is exempt from property tax.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005, the Sudanese government of National Unity (GNU) named a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox" title="Coptic Orthodox">
       Coptic Orthodox
      </a>
      priest to a government position, though the ruling Islamist party's continued dominance under the GNU provides ample reason to doubt its commitment to broader religious or ethnic representation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Copts_in_modern_Libya">
       Copts in modern Libya
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Libya" title="Copts in Libya">
       Copts in Libya
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Libya" title="Christianity in Libya">
       Christianity in Libya
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The largest Christian group in Libya is the
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">
       Coptic Orthodox Church
      </a>
      , with a population of 60,000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-multiple-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Coptic Church is known to have historical roots in Libya long before the Arabs advanced westward from Egypt into Libya.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Egypt" title="Christianity in Egypt">
       Christianity in Egypt
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Sudan" title="Christianity in Sudan">
       Christianity in Sudan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Libya" title="Christianity in Libya">
       Christianity in Libya
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Living in countries with Muslim majorities (Egypt, Sudan, Libya), the size of the population of Copts is a continuously disputed matter, frequently for reasons of religious jealousy and animosity.
     </p>
     <p>
      The ethnic Coptic population
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copts_in_Egypt" title="Copts in Egypt">
       in Egypt
      </a>
      is difficult to estimate but some official estimates state that Coptic Christians represent from 5% to 10% or less of a population of over 83 million Egyptians
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_world_factbook.2FEgypt.2F_26-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_world_factbook.2FEgypt.2F-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPS_News_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-IPS_News-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christianpost.com_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-christianpost.com-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_Institute_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Washington_Institute-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nlgsolutions1_30-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nlgsolutions1-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt_20-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO.2FEgypt.2F_21-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-FCO.2FEgypt.2F-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msn_encarta.2FEgypt_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-msn_encarta.2FEgypt-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while other independent and Christian sources estimate much higher numbers, up to 23% of the population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt_20-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-U.S.Dept_of_State.2FEgypt-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FCO.2FEgypt.2F_21-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-FCO.2FEgypt.2F-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_world_factbook.2FEgypt.2F_26-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_world_factbook.2FEgypt.2F-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPS_News_27-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-IPS_News-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christianpost.com_28-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-christianpost.com-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtoninstitute.org_29-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-washingtoninstitute.org-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nlgsolutions1_30-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-nlgsolutions1-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msn_encarta.2FEgypt_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-msn_encarta.2FEgypt-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The ethnic Coptic population
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Sudan" title="Copts in Sudan">
       in Sudan
      </a>
      is at about half a million or 1% of Sudanese population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr1_4-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-unhcr1-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The ethnic Coptic population
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Libya" title="Copts in Libya">
       in Libya
      </a>
      is about over 60,000 or 1% of Libyan population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">
       Diaspora
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_diaspora" title="Coptic diaspora">
       Coptic diaspora
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG/180px-StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG/270px-StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG/360px-StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG 2x" width="180"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StMarkCopticOrthodoxChurchBellaireTX0.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        St. Mark Coptic Orthodox Church in
        <a href="/wiki/Bellaire,_Texas" title="Bellaire, Texas">
         Bellaire, Texas
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">
         Greater Houston
        </a>
        ). There are about 1-2 million Copts living outside of Egypt, and are known as the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Coptic_diaspora" title="Coptic diaspora">
          Coptic diaspora
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Outside of the Coptic primary area of residence within parts of present day Egypt, Sudan (
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Sudan" title="Copts in Sudan">
       Copts in Sudan
      </a>
      ), and Libya (
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Libya" title="Copts in Libya">
       Copts in Libya
      </a>
      ), the largest ethnic Coptic diaspora population is located within the United States, Canada, and Australia. The numbers of the Censuses in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
       Canada
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
       Australia
      </a>
      are not fully correct since many ethnic Copts listed themselves in the 2011 Census mistakenly as either Egyptians, Sudanese, Libyans, Americans, Canadians or Australians and by this way reducing the ethnic Coptic population in the 2011 Census in the United States, Canada, and Australia respectively.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nevertheless, the ethnic
      <a href="/wiki/Coptic_American" title="Coptic American">
       Coptic American
      </a>
      population is estimate to number about 200,000 (estimates of Coptic organizations ranging as high as a million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009_American_Community_Survey_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-2009_American_Community_Survey-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_Tribune_2007_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh_Tribune_2007-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JS_Online_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-JS_Online-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US-Copts_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-US-Copts-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ethnic
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Canada" title="Copts in Canada">
       Coptic Canadian
      </a>
      population is estimate to number about 50,000
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (estimates of Coptic organizations ranging as high as 200,000).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montreal_Gazette_1-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Montreal_Gazette-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elaph.com_11-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-elaph.com-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ethnic
      <a href="/wiki/Copts_in_Australia" title="Copts in Australia">
       Coptic Australian
      </a>
      population is estimate to number about 50,000
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parliament.nsw.gov.au_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-parliament.nsw.gov.au-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coptic.org.au_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-coptic.org.au-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (estimates of Coptic organizations ranging as high as 100,000).
     </p>
     <p>
      Smaller communities (below 50,000) are found in
      <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">
       Kuwait
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the United Kingdom,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      France,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      South Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Come_Across_And_Help_Us_Book_2_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Come_Across_And_Help_Us_Book_2-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CopticMission_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CopticMission-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Minor communities below 10,000 people are reported from
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Jordan
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Germany,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Switzerland,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Austria,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and elsewhere.
     </p>
     <p>
      It is noted that ethnic Copts also live in Lebanon, Denmark, Greece, Italy, the Netherlands, Norway, Russia, and Sweden.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
